Statistic with R

Chapter 3 Sampling Distribution

3.1 Sampling

3.1.1 Simple Random Sampling

Sampling from 1 to 10, sample size = 5

Simple random sampling with replacement

sample(x = 1:10,size = 5, replace = TRUE)
## [1] 10  6  5  9  5

Simple random sampling without replacement

sample(x = 1:10,size = 5, replace = FALSE)
## [1]  6  4  2  7 10

If we want to sample 10 cars from mtcars dataset and stratified by cylâ€¦

The easiest way to do stratified sampling is using strata function from sampling package. If you never install sampling package, you need to install it install.package("sampling") first.

library(sampling)
sample_n<-round(table(mtcars$cyl)/(nrow(mtcars)/10),0)
strata(mtcars,stratanames = "cyl",size = sample_n)
## Warning in strata(mtcars, stratanames = "cyl", size = sample_n): the method is
## not specified; by default, the method is srswor
##    cyl ID_unit      Prob Stratum
## 2    6       2 0.4285714       1
## 6    6       6 0.4285714       1
## 11   6      11 0.4285714       1
## 18   4      18 0.1818182       2
## 26   4      26 0.1818182       2
## 13   8      13 0.2857143       3
## 14   8      14 0.2857143       3
## 17   8      17 0.2857143       3
## 31   8      31 0.2857143       3

The distribution of iris Sepal.Length

hist(iris$Sepal.Length)

The descriptive analysis of iris Sepal.Length (population)

mean(iris$Sepal.Length)
## [1] 5.843333
sd.p(iris$Sepal.Length)
## [1] 0.8253013

If we randomly sample 5 record from iris Sepal.Length

s_5<-sample(iris$Sepal.Length,5,replace = T)
s_5
## [1] 5.8 5.6 6.4 6.7 7.7

The mean and sd of the sampling results (one time)

mean(s_5)
## [1] 6.44
sd(s_5)
## [1] 0.8324662

3.3 Sampling Distribution of the Sample Mean

If the population is 1 to 10, we can have population mean and sd

mean(1:10)
## [1] 5.5
sd.p(1:10)
## [1] 2.872281

If we randomly sample 5 record from 1 to 10

s_5<-sample(1:10,5,replace = T)
s_5
## [1] 4 3 7 9 3

The mean and sd of the sampling results (one time)

mean(s_5)
## [1] 5.2
sd(s_5)
## [1] 2.683282

If we sample 5 cases from 1 to 10, how many combinations will have?

allComb<-
  do.call(data.table::CJ, 
          replicate(5, 1:10, simplify = FALSE))
nrow(allComb)
## [1] 100000
head(allComb,10)
##     V1 V2 V3 V4 V5

For the sample mean we have, we can visualize the distribution, caculate mean and sd for the sample mean

hist(rowMeans(allComb))

mean(rowMeans(allComb))
## [1] 5.5
sd.p(rowMeans(allComb))
## [1] 1.284523

Compare population mean/sd with sample mean mean/sd

The population mean = mean of sample mean

mean(1:10)
## [1] 5.5
mean(rowMeans(allComb))
## [1] 5.5

The population sd != sd of sample mean

sd.p(1:10)
## [1] 2.872281
sd.p(rowMeans(allComb))
## [1] 1.284523

But, from the classâ€¦.we know that \[ \sigma _\bar{x} = \sigma / \sqrt{n} \]

We have \[ \sigma / \sqrt{n} \]

sd.p(1:10)/(5^(1/2))
## [1] 1.284523

Then \[ \sigma _\bar{x} \]

sd.p(rowMeans(allComb))
## [1] 1.284523
